Lawsuit Against Village Head for Hiding the Bride: Illegal Kidnapping: He Jiping Confronted, He Xianjuan Appears 121

Zhou Siquan, a farmer from Mashaqiao Shayou Township in Shanghai County, is 26 years old. When he was young, his parents arranged for him to marry He Xianjuan, the daughter of He Heshang from the same village, through a matchmaker. They chose the 21st day of the tenth month of the old calendar this year to get married. When the auspicious day arrived, Zhou Siquan prepared gongs and drums, and a colorful sedan chair to go to the bride's house to welcome her. Unexpectedly, the bride could not be found. The sudden change on the eve of the wedding was extremely surprising. The festive event was spoiled. He took his father-in-law to the Third Police Station for reasoning. Then, the original matchmaker, Yang Jinyun, rushed to say that the bride had been hidden by He Jiping, the village head of the township, and her intentions were unknown. The police chief immediately ordered the senior police officer to go to the address and bring He Jiping and the bride He Xianjuan to the station together. After persuasion by relatives and friends, both parties calmed down. He Jiping was confronted, and He Xianjuan was taken back by Zhou Siquan in the sedan chair. However, the auspicious day had been missed, and it was agreed to change the date for the wedding. However, He Jiping, who suffered this humiliation, was unwilling and filed a complaint with the Shanghai County Public Security Bureau, accusing Zhou Siquan of instigating Wang Musheng, Fei Yuehua, Zhou Shulin, and others to illegally kidnap the bride. The bureau ordered the police to detain the four people and send them to the Shanghai District Court. After the prosecutor inquired about the previous situation, he released Zhou and others. After Zhou and others were released, they were very angry and hired lawyer Yang Yiming to countersue for false accusation and obstruction of family.

New Jiangtian Steamer Causes Accident in Ningbo: Negotiations for Compensation: Careless Turning Damages Three Civilian Boats: Losses of Several Hundred Dollars, China Merchants Bureau Pays Compensation 122

Datong News Agency reported that the China Merchants Bureau's New Jiangtian steamer sailed from Shanghai to Ningbo on the morning of the 9th. Due to careless turning, it damaged three civilian boats. It is reported that the Ningbo Civilian Boat Industry Workers' Union has sent a letter to the China Merchants Bureau to negotiate compensation. The original letter is recorded below:

On the morning of the 9th of this month at 8 a.m., member Fan Yunchao and others of the short-haul boat reported to the association, stating that the members' barges had finished unloading and were docked to the right front of the New Beijing wharf. Unexpectedly, at around 6 a.m. today, the New Jiangtian steamer entered the port and exceeded the fixed anchorage. "At that time, the tide was rising, and instead of dropping the front anchor, they rashly turned the ship to dock. The tide was so rapid at this time that the power of navigation was ineffective. As a result, the ship crossed the river to the opposite side of the Datong Hotel before turning around. At this time, if the ship could maintain a fixed position, there would be no risk of collision with the members' barges. Who knew that at this time, the stern of the ship suddenly slanted into the river bank? The second mate, who was in charge of observing safety at the stern of the ship, clearly knew that the members' ships were in a dangerous situation where they could not avoid it. He did not notify the engine room to stop the ship, causing the three barges of the members to be violently hit and sunk by the stern of the ship. Subsequently, someone was entrusted to salvage the sunken ship. After an estimate of the damage by a shipwright, it was said that it would cost more than 800 yuan to repair. The livelihood of several members of the family depends on this barge transportation. Now, they have suffered this unexpected accident for no reason, and their livelihood is worrying," etc. After sending personnel to the scene of the accident for thorough investigation, it was reported that the barges of member Fan Yunchao and others were indeed docked to the right end of the New Beijing wharf. It was found that the distance between that place and the New Jiangtian steamer wharf was more than 520 meters. If the captain was not careless and able to drop anchor at a fixed anchorage, and the second mate in charge of observing safety at the stern of the ship could fulfill his duties, there would be no reason for the collision. It is clear that the fault lies with the steamer, not the barges," etc. Based on this, we hereby request your bureau to investigate and compensate for the damage in accordance with the provisions of Article 113 of the Maritime Law, in order to alleviate the hardships of the workers.

Then, the Chinese and Western detectives reported the process of detaining the defendant. When questioned, Zheng Wenkui's confession was evasive. Judge Xiao Xieffen ordered him to be returned to custody and rescheduled for further verification.

Ma Kunle Commits Suicide with a Suicide Note: Comes to Shanghai to Seek a Job, Fails to Achieve Anything: Suicide Due to Unemployment, No One Else to Blame 125

Ma Kunle from Guizhou, 31 years old, used to work in the military. After retiring, he came to Shanghai to seek a job, but achieved nothing, causing him to wander around Shanghai. He was in a foreign land and it was now midwinter. He was hungry and cold and could not return home, leading to his short-sightedness. At 9 p.m. on the 12th, he went to the Fuxing Inn at No. 72 Avenue Joffre in the French Concession and checked into Room No. 6 on the pretext of borrowing a room. That night, he committed suicide by taking poison. At 7 a.m. yesterday, the tea attendant entered the room to empty the chamber pot and found that Ma had died on the bed. He immediately reported it to the Avenue Joffre Police Station. Detectives were dispatched to investigate and found a suicide note written in pencil on a letter paper near the pillow, "To the public service, suicide due to unemployment, no one else to blame, life is boring, please do not rescue, Guizhou native, 31 years old, Ma Kunle from the military, suicide note, " In a few words, the body was sent to the Tongren Fuyuan branch morgue for examination. The suicide note was taken back to the police station and reported to the head of the police, waiting for the Second Special District Court to examine it today.

Apprentice Chen Bianpin Dies Suddenly: Father Requests Investigation to Seek Justice: Factory Owner Suspected, Sent to the Bureau for Investigation 128

Chen Dianrong, 44 years old, from Wuxi, lives at No. 320 Fuyou Road in the city. His son, Chen Xiepin, 17 years old, was introduced by Chen Qiyuan in the spring of the 23rd year of the Republic of China and worked as an apprentice at the Huiming Dry Battery Factory opened by Ding Rongzhao at No. 58 Runan Street, Zhaoban Road, Shanghai South. For more than two years, he has been subjected to abuse by foreman Yin Yuzhang and others (28 years old, from Tongzhou, living at No. 5 Changyuanli, Qu Zhenren Road). Although the original introducer and others repeatedly dissuaded them, it was still ineffective. Unexpectedly, at 12 a.m. on the 9th of this month, Chen Xiepin suddenly died in the factory. The factory owner, Ding Rongzhao, paid 26 yuan to prepare a coffin for burial. The deceased's father, Chen Dianrong, believes that the sudden death of his son is unclear, and yesterday he submitted a petition to the Ximen Public Security Bureau, requesting an investigation to seek justice. Chief Yao Guangnai approved it and immediately ordered the original witnesses to be brought to the case for detailed interrogation. According to foreman Ji Yuzhang, he was not at the factory on the night of the 9th. He only found out after apprentice Chen Xiepin died. The rest of his words were evasive. According to accountant He Yubin, the apprentice reported to the factory owner after his death, and the factory owner paid for the burial. Another apprentice, Lin Wenbin, said that he slept on a two-story bed with the deceased. On the night of the 9th, the deceased fell from the upper bed and died. Finally, according to the original introducer Chen Qiyuan, who claimed to be the former factory director of the factory, the deceased was introduced by him. Usually, the factory owner treated him harshly, so he often came to cry and wanted to quit. I advised him to be patient and learn his skills. That night, the factory sent two people to say that Chen Xiepin was seriously ill and was quickly sent to the hospital. It was not until the next morning that he found out he had died. After reviewing the confession, the bureau believes that the case involves allegations of abuse and resulted in death. It is believed that the factory owner, Ding Rongzhao, is highly suspected. In addition to first ordering the local security officer to go to the local court for an examination, the police were also dispatched to continue summoning the factory owner to the case for questioning, and the witnesses' original petitions and guarantees were prepared and sent to the Public Security Bureau for review.

Measurement Bureau Notice: Hong Kong No-Anchoring Area, Shantou Luyu Outer Limit Light Installation 130

The Shanghai Hydrographic Survey Bureau issued two notices to indicate the no-anchoring area for ships in Hong Kong and the establishment of range lights on Luyu Island in Shantou. The following is a separate record:

Hong Kong No-Anchoring Area

Notice No. 2, Hong Kong No-Anchoring Area: (1) Position: (A) Six degrees, distance 1.08 nautical miles; (B) Forty-one degrees, distance 1.28 nautical miles, from Green Island Lighthouse, approximately 114 degrees 7 minutes East longitude and 22 degrees 18 minutes North latitude. (2) Explanation: No anchoring is allowed between the lit buoys at this location. The words "No Anchoring" are marked on the chart at the above (A) and (B) positions. (3) Related charts: British Admiralty Charts No. 3228 and No. 14.6. (4) Original reporting agency: British Shipping Notice No. 1915 of this year.

Shantou Range Light Installation

Shantou Port Luyu Island "Outer Limit Range Lights Outside Muyu Fish Weir" Installation: (A) Front (low) light (1) Position: 56.75 degrees from the Xintingshan, distance 8.65 chains, namely 116 degrees 45 minutes East longitude and 23 degrees 30 minutes North latitude. (1) Light quality: One fixed white light. (B) Rear (high) light: (1) Position: 63.75 degrees from the Qishan, distance 9.2 chains. (2) Light quality: One fixed white light. Note: When the two lights are in line, the bearing is 126.75 degrees, indicating the location of the western end of the 1.5 chain fish weir southwest of Muyu in the Luyu harbor channel. Related charts: Navy Department Hydrographic Chart No. 97. This light should be included in the first edition of the Navy Department's Coastal Lighthouse List as No. 94A and No. 94B. Original reporting agency: Shantou Port Director.

Dredging Bureau Adds Large Dredger, As Huge As the Jianshe, Contractor Can Be Determined Soon, Construction Takes One and a Half Years to Complete 131

The Shanghai Dredging Bureau, in order to dredge the Xintan outside Wusongkou, has ordered the construction of a giant dredger called "Jianshe" from Germany. It arrived in Shanghai in April last year and immediately sailed to the shoal to start dredging. The work is proceeding smoothly, as reported in the newspapers. According to a reporter from Datong News Agency, in order to ensure that the dredging project of the shoal is completed within five years as scheduled, the bureau has invited shipbuilders from various countries to bid for the construction of a dredger of the same size as the "Jianshe." Shipbuilders from various countries have already submitted bids to the bureau, so Chief Engineer Dr. Chatley will soon select one of them for construction. It will take about a year and a half to complete the work, launch the vessel, and sail it to Shanghai for delivery.

Hongkou Empty, Tenants' Association Sends Letter to Municipal Council Requesting Winter House Rent Exemption and Compassion 135

The City Tenants' Association sent a letter to the Municipal Council yesterday, stating: "We are writing to inform you that the market has been depressed in recent years, and all sectors of industry and commerce are deeply distressed. Hongkou District suffered severely during the January 28th Incident because it was adjacent to the war zone. The Haining Road Incident occurred, and Japanese troops set up sentry posts and armed patrols. Residents were intimidated by their power and moved away, resulting in the tragic situation of 'nine out of ten houses being empty.' The industrial and commercial sectors have also declined further. Today, the second landlords in Hongkou District have many vacant houses, and the rent paid is suffering huge losses, while the quarterly house rent is particularly burdensome. Tenant after tenant in that neighborhood has come to the association to complain about their suffering, requesting rent reduction or rent exemption, and their pleas are sincere and cannot be ignored. Therefore, the association has resolved that Hongkou District has been most severely affected by the economic downturn. Under these extraordinary circumstances, the Municipal Council should exempt winter house rent to alleviate the burden on tenants, to show compassion in the face of hardship. We hereby submit this request, hoping that you will consider the difficult times and approve the exemption of winter house rent in Hongkou District, to alleviate the hardship and show compassion."

Guo Shunlin, Adultery with a Married Woman, Eight Months Imprisonment Suspended for Three Years, Must Pay More Than One Hundred and Forty Yuan in Fines 140

Tao Zhirong, a Suzhou native and brother-in-law of the slide opera singer Zhang Yizhi, married Yin Shuhua, a woman from his hometown, in 1933. They lived harmoniously until August 6 of this year, when Yin suddenly left home. She sent a letter through a lawyer to Tao, claiming that she could not bear the abuse and requested a reasonable settlement. Tao ignored it and filed a lawsuit in the Special Second Court against Yin, requesting reconciliation for cohabitation. Yin could not be found. After posting a reward and advertising in the newspapers, someone informed him that Yin was living with Guo Shunlin, a young man from Changzhou, in Yili No. 15, Belle Road. Tao reported it to the French Concession police, who dispatched detectives Jiang Guo and Yin and arrested them. They were sent to the Criminal Division of the Special Second Court and prosecuted for adultery. As a result of the trial, Guo was sentenced to three months of imprisonment and Yin to two months of imprisonment, each suspended for two years. The details have been reported in this newspaper. The Police Affairs Department of the French Concession expressed dissatisfaction with the light sentence imposed on Guo and filed an appeal to the High Third Branch Court. The appeal has now been concluded, and the original judgment regarding Guo Shunlin's crime has been revoked. Guo Shunlin has been re-sentenced to eight months of imprisonment, suspended for three years. However, Tao's lawsuit against Yin for cohabitation has been mediated out of court, and the two parties have divorced. Tao has withdrawn the lawsuit. But Tao has suffered a reward and advertising loss of more than 140 yuan due to Guo's seduction and concealment of his wife, Yin Shuhua. Tao, represented by lawyer Wang Hengyi, filed a lawsuit against Guo in the Special Second Court for damages. There have been two court hearings, but the criminal appeal case has been put on hold. Now that the appeal case has been adjudicated, the civil case will proceed again.

Use of Counterfeit Money Investigated 141

Zhang Ashan, a native of Changshu, 27 years old, used a counterfeit five-yuan bill and two one-yuan bills from the Central Bank at Rongchang Cigarette and Paper Shop at No. 848 Zhoujiazui Road between 3 PM and 5 PM on the ninth of this month and escaped. The apprentice Qian Jindou found him in a nearby teahouse at noon the day before yesterday. He reported it, and the Chinese constable from No. 98 came and arrested him at the Huishan Police Station. He was sent to the Criminal Third Court of the First Special District Court yesterday. Judge Zhong questioned him and denied it. He was ordered to be detained and the case was adjourned for further investigation.

Lawyer Shen Xiaoxiang Sentenced to One Year for False Accusation, Result of Handwriting Analysis 142

Lawyer Shen Xiaoxiang, a native of Minhou, Fujian, has his office and residence at No. 7 Jinyi Lane, Jielu. This year, Shen represented Zhao Minzhou and Tang Liye from Jiangbei in accusing Che Lisheng of fraud and exploitation of usurious interest. Later, Che Lisheng was acquitted by the local court. In August, the court suddenly received a letter attacking the original judge for taking bribes and violating the law. The court immediately dispatched the late clerk Xuan Maohe to investigate. Shen Xiaoxiang was suspected of writing the letter. Shen was released on bail and his handwriting was found to be the same. He was prosecuted for false accusation. Judge Wang Junyi opened a trial and questioned him. Shen Xiaoxiang claimed that Wei Ziqiu had imitated his handwriting to frame him. The interrogator had Shen's handwriting and Wei's handwriting compared with the original letter by calligrapher Wang Xishen, and it still matched Shen Xiaoxiang's. The case was confirmed, and the sentence was announced yesterday: Shen Xiaoxiang was sentenced to one year of imprisonment for false accusation and deprived of his civil rights for five years.

Ding Manli Attempts Suicide by Poisoning, Critically Ill 145

Ding Manli, the 19-year-old daughter of Ding Shunyuan, a native of Haiyan, Zhejiang, residing at No. 67 Matianxing Lane in Nanshi, was betrothed this spring to a Mr. Qian (the same age as the girl), who is studying at a university in Huxi. They had a love match since childhood. Although they were not yet married, the young couple had a close relationship and visited each other frequently. Recently, the girl, for some unknown reason, suddenly had a suicidal thought. Yesterday morning, she swallowed poison at home. After taking the poison, she still lay in bed. At 9 o'clock, her mother saw that she was still sleeping in bed and called her without response. She lifted the curtain and saw that the girl's face had turned pale and she could not speak. She also saw traces of raw opium on the girl's fingers and corners of her mouth, and realized that she had taken poison. She immediately hired a car and rushed her to the hospital for emergency treatment. According to the doctor, because the poisoning was too deep, there was little hope of survival.

Young Woman Hangs Herself in Resentment, Husband Must Act as a Filial Son, Only Then Will the Mother's Family Be Satisfied 148

Jin Bukui from Yancheng, lives in a thatched shed without a number at the south end of the Bingchang Tian in Pudong. He is now a foreman at the Yongtai Wharf in Lujiazui. His first wife died and left a son, Rongshan, 17 years old, who is also a worker at the wharf. Last October, he married Nian Qiao, the daughter of Xia Yutian from Shanyang, through a matchmaker. She was only 16 years old at the time. The young couple had no love for each other, and Jin's stepmother, Chen, was extremely fierce and regarded Nian Qiao as a thorn in her side. At 11 AM the day before yesterday, Chen quarreled with her again over a trivial matter. Nian Qiao was so angry that she pretended to go to the room to remove the bed curtains for washing. After a while, there was still no movement. Chen went into the room to check and saw Nian Qiao hanging herself on the bamboo beam. She had already died. At this time, Jin and his son also returned home from work and were shocked to see the scene. They immediately sent someone to notify the dead woman's family. Jin, fearing that he would be convicted, went to the Pudong Sub-Bureau and falsely reported that she had died of illness. The bureau officers noticed his panicked expression and became suspicious. They immediately sent police to investigate and learned the truth. He was taken to the bureau for interrogation for falsely reporting a murder case, and Nian Qiao's mother's family also went to ask for justice, believing that she had been forced to commit suicide. Jin was interrogated by the sub-bureau and found to be innocent. That night, he was released on bail. Jin then asked relatives and friends to persuade his in-laws, promising to give the dead woman a generous funeral and ordering Rongshan (that is, the dead woman's husband) to act as a filial son and personally attend the funeral. Only then was the other party satisfied. Yesterday morning, the sub-bureau ordered Dibao Lu Shunlong to report to the court for inspection. At the same time, the father of the deceased, Yutian, also petitioned the court for exemption from inspection. The court approved it. At the time of the funeral that afternoon, the husband wore mourning clothes and behaved as if he had lost his parents. The onlookers were amazed.

New Pharmaceutical Industry Federation Requests Exemption from Inspection of Imported Medicines 154

The National Federation of New Pharmaceutical Industry Associations submitted a petition to the Ministry of Finance, stating that it was petitioning for the removal of the "medicines" category from the list of items subject to inspection for imported goods, in order to alleviate the difficulties of businesses. It stated that the government, in order to prevent the import of smuggled goods and maintain national tax revenue, had promulgated the "Provisional Regulations for Inspection of Imported Goods Transportation and Sales" and specified the types of goods subject to inspection. Initially, there were twenty-six categories, none of which included medicines. Later, when the revised list of imported goods subject to inspection was promulgated, medicines were added. Consequently, the goods of our new pharmaceutical industry are also subject to inspection. However, the term "medicines" encompasses both Chinese and Western medicines. Considering only Western medicines, there are statistically no fewer than sixty to seventy thousand types. The Ministry has not clearly indicated which types should be inspected, causing all businesses, whether manufacturing or selling, to apply for licenses according to regulations. The procedures are cumbersome and often time-consuming. Medicines are essential for medical treatment and are vital to human life. If urgently needed medicines are delayed due to licensing procedures, it is indirectly harmful to society. Except for domestically produced Western medicines, 99% come from Europe and America. Now, both goods manufactured by Chinese merchants and those entirely produced in Europe and America, which have no possibility of being smuggled, are being inspected uniformly. This is unfairly impacting innocent parties. Therefore, according to the resolution of the first national member representative conference of the affiliated association, we respectfully submit this petition to the Ministry, hoping that you will consider the people's hardships and grant permission to remove the "medicines" category from the list of imported goods subject to inspection, and order its implementation to alleviate the difficulties of businesses. This would be a great act of kindness.

The exhibition featured a total of two hundred and fifty-seven pieces.

Economic Special

Observations on the Future of the Pound Sterling 165

— Bao Yuchi

Since the devaluation of the French franc, the monetary agreement between the United Kingdom, the United States, and France, and the gold export agreement between the three countries, the world monetary war seems to have come to a halt. What impact will these two new monetary agreements have on the future of the pound sterling? At the same time, what policies will the UK's Exchange Equalisation Account adopt to adjust exchange rates? These are the current urgent issues for British currency that need to be resolved. If the contents of the three-nation currency agreement do not stipulate the premium between London and New York, it can be said to be meaningless; in other words, the exchange rate between the pound and the dollar must have a limited regulation. If the price of gold calculated in pounds fluctuates without limit, the United States will certainly not participate in the agreement. Assuming that the above two currency agreements will stipulate the limits of the pound-dollar exchange rate, it is necessary to describe the past environment and policies of British currency when reviewing the future of the pound sterling.

Since 1931, the elements that determine the pound exchange rate are not only the UK's trade balance and international balance of payments, but also the total trade balance between the sterling area and other countries in the world. Because London has regained its world financial hegemony in the past five years and has become the center of international lending and the hub of financial regulation and clearing for sterling area countries. This factual formation is due in part to the stability of the pound price; in part to the need for countries in the sterling area to maintain liquidity in the London market for allocation. The countries in the sterling area ship goods to London quarterly and use the proceeds from the sale of goods to store in London, so the liquidity in London is increasing daily. However, countries in the sterling area are also likely to export gold and liquidity stored in London due to the payment of goods imported from other countries and for other reasons, which will affect the rise and fall of the pound exchange rate.

For example, in 1935, the United Kingdom owed foreign countries approximately £205 million, which is only the figure for the merchandise import surplus; in addition, it owed sterling area countries a total of £73 million; at the same time, in 1935, the United Kingdom had intangible exports to sterling area countries totaling £150 million. Balancing the two, the United Kingdom actually held a claim of £80 million. Countries in the sterling area can offset part of the UK's import surplus by shipping goods overseas and receiving payment for them. Therefore, the invisible export item in the UK's international trade plays an important role and can also have a serious impact on the rise and fall of the pound exchange rate. Under the shadow of the recession in the past few years, non-commodity items in the UK's international balance of payments, such as gold flows, capital movements, and freight, have been undergoing obvious changes year by year and have gradually become important. This evolution of facts can often have a powerful impact on the pound sterling, whether the movement of gold and capital occurs within the sterling area or between the sterling area and other countries, it has the same impact on the pound sterling, but the results are different. Last year, the surge in prices, the moderate recovery of world trade, the recovery of shipping, and the abnormal development of international speculative funds pouring into Wall Street in the United States were all sufficient to influence the rise and fall of the pound price, making the work of the UK's Exchange Equalisation Account increasingly complex and difficult.

Today, the work of the UK's Exchange Equalisation Account is even more difficult. Because London's foreign lending is prohibited, and the British authorities are actively promoting a cheap money policy, the steps to maintain the pound exchange rate are far less simple than in the past. The war clouds are spreading in Europe, and the international situation is becoming increasingly tense. The production of British steel and machinery is insufficient for application, and it has to be imported from foreign countries, so the figures for merchandise import surplus are expanding daily. The figures for this year's import surplus have already exceeded £55 million compared to the same period last year. However, as far as the UK itself is concerned, there is no major danger. Because the UK's international balance of payments last year had a credit balance of £40 million; and the UK's overseas loans are due for repayment every year. In 1933, the most recessionary year, the inflow of British overseas funds was estimated to be as high as £67 million. The figures for this year are also around £80 million. The result of the inflow of funds has had a good impact on the pound sterling, and London's liquidity has been quite active. The inflow of funds has always been listed as a non-commodity item and is a kind of intangible income.

As mentioned above, the British authorities should pay close attention to this item of intangible income. There are many sources of this income, and the threads are complicated, including interest on overseas investment, freight, and miscellaneous labor services. The interest on overseas investment was estimated at approximately £160 million in 1934, and the figure estimated by the Ministry of Commerce in 1935 was also £170 million. Freight was estimated at approximately £70 million in 1935. Other miscellaneous income, such as the sale of ships, government transactions, etc., is also between £40 million and £50 million. Therefore, the UK's intangible income occupies an important position in the international balance of payments due to the large amount, which cannot be denied. And it is also an iron fact that it can indirectly affect the future of the pound sterling. Recently, due to the devaluation of various countries' currencies, the softening of import quota systems, and the removal of tariff barriers, the economic situation of various countries seems to be showing signs of prosperity; then the interest income of British overseas investment may be able to increase from £170 million in 1935 to the pre-panic level of £300 million, which is obviously very beneficial to the situation of the pound sterling.

In the current situation, if the UK does not find a way to increase trade with non-sterling area countries, then the future of the pound sterling has two major potential dangers: the first is that British funds may flow out due to the attraction of the New York Stock Exchange in the United States; the second is the increase in merchandise import surplus. In the past, gold standard countries, because of the occurrence of domestic panic, the funds stored in London are now gradually flowing out and returning, which is insignificant and can be handled and dealt with easily by the UK's Exchange Equalisation Account. The funds flowing to Wall Street can also be easily stopped through strict adjustment and management. Only increasing the export of goods is indeed a difficult problem to solve. According to experts' estimates, this year's merchandise import surplus will exceed last year's by more than £75 million, and the actual excess figure may be even greater. The increase in overseas investment income is only about £10 million to £20 million; and the increase in freight income is only about £10 million to £15 million. The only remaining income that can offset the import surplus is capital movement. Capital movement is already an important factor determining the strength of the pound sterling.

Based on the above description, the future of the pound sterling is very critical. If Wall Street can remain stable and no longer cause trouble in the near future, then the pound sterling should be able to return to stability within this year. However, the future of the United States in 1937, newly devalued countries, and the world commodity market is unknowable, so the good or bad of the future of the pound sterling cannot be determined in advance. However, it is already a clear and undeniable fact that the work of the UK's Exchange Equalisation Account will become more difficult.

Since the pound sterling joined the three-nation currency agreement and signed the gentlemen's agreement, the pound exchange rate should not have severe ups and downs in recent months. The exchange rate against the US dollar has recently been fluctuating around 4 shillings and 89 pence, which seems too high; if intangible income cannot have a substantial increase, then the US-UK exchange rate will have the opposite development. Therefore, it is best if the gold prices of various countries can obtain a reasonable export and import point. The United States, France, Switzerland, and other countries have already made regulations. If the United Kingdom can also stipulate a limit, and add tax cuts and cooperation of the exchange equalization fund, not only can the currencies of ____ countries step onto the road to prosperity, but the entire world monetary system can also lay a sound foundation.

A Review of Small-Amount Credit Loans from Banks 166

— Tang Tongsun

(I) An Outline of General Banking Operations

The establishment of banks is a product of modern social group living. They bear the responsibility of regulating finance, and their business revolves around the supply and demand of funds. However, we must understand that banks are a necessary component of a modern economic society. We must first briefly discuss the business operations of banks before discussing the small-amount credit loan business that this article intends to discuss.

Simply put, banks mainly engage in two major businesses: deposits and loans. Other businesses, such as remittances and trusts, the former is merely to regulate finance between two locations, helping the bank to achieve its mission. The latter is the bank relying on its own capabilities as a credit institution to serve customers.

(A) Deposits are the lifeblood of banks. In short, the reason why banks can regulate surplus funds is only because they can use deposits to lend to those who lack funds. There are five types of deposits:

(1) Current Deposits

1. Current deposits at commercial banks

2. Current deposits at savings banks

(2) Time Deposits

1. Compound interest deposits (i.e., lump-sum deposit and lump-sum withdrawal)

2. Installment deposits and lump-sum withdrawal

3. Lump-sum deposit and installment withdrawal

4. Principal deposit with interest payments

(3) Notice Deposits

(4) Bill Deposits

(5) Temporary Deposits

Current deposits at banks do not actually generate any profit for the bank itself. They require sufficient reserves for immediate payment and involve complicated procedures. However, they offer great convenience to depositors. Merchants and companies, whose daily income is in silver, would inevitably face the risk of unforeseen circumstances if they kept it themselves. Therefore, once deposited in a bank as a current deposit, they do not need to bear the risk of safekeeping, payment is convenient, and they can also earn some interest. Why wouldn't they do it? For the banks themselves, since their mission is to regulate finance, they cannot complain about complicated procedures.

Then there are time deposits. Depositors in this area can generally be divided into the following types:

(1) Those who have funds but lack investment experience;

(2) Ordinary workers whose earnings are very small, so they save bit by bit in the hope of accumulating more.

Because this type of deposit does not require reserves, it can be fully utilized. Therefore, time deposits are the largest source of funds for banks.

Other deposits, such as bill deposits, notice deposits, and temporary deposits, are merely methods used by banks to attract funds!

(B) Loans – broadly speaking, there are three types of loans:

(1) Bill Discounting

(2) Mortgage Loans

1. Real estate mortgage loans

2. Chattel mortgage loans

(3) Credit Loans

1. Secured credit loans

2. Unsecured credit loans

As mentioned earlier, banks absorb and concentrate funds from all parties and then distribute funds. Therefore, the lending business is a method of distributing funds.

The meaning of discounting is that the bank buys bills that have not yet matured. From the date of purchase to the maturity date, the interest to be deducted is calculated at the current market interest rate, and the cash is exchanged for the bill holder. There are five types of bills that ordinary banks discount:

(1) Bills issued by producers or manufacturers to wholesalers;

(2) Bills issued by wholesalers to retailers;

(3) Bills issued by consumers to retailers;

(4) Bank drafts, bills of exchange, and money shop drafts and bills of exchange.

The first, second, and third types of bills listed above are the commercial acceptance drafts and various import and export bills of exchange currently processed by banks; the fourth type of bill is the most common discounted bill on the market.

Discounted loans generally have very short terms, while longer-term loans are only mortgage loans and credit loans. Among mortgage loans, real estate mortgage loans have longer terms. These loans are mostly secured by factory foundations, land, houses, and equipment; chattel loans are mostly secured by commodities, government bonds, stocks, corporate bonds, gold and silver, etc. Secondly, regarding credit loans, one type is secured credit loans, and the other is unsecured credit loans. The formation of this type of loan had already reached its peak in our country during the era of money shops. For hundreds of years, the regulation of domestic agriculture and commerce in our country has relied entirely on credit loans from money shops. However, since the opening of maritime trade, foreign financial institutions have mainly focused on exchange and mortgage loans. In addition, in recent years, the global economic downturn has permeated China, and this type of credit loan has greatly diminished in importance.

(II) The Reasons and Methods for Banks to Establish Small-Amount Credit Loans

Banks are using all their ingenuity to attract business in order to absorb funds. They have established various savings deposit methods to absorb small amounts from individuals. Thus, on the one hand, banks have reached the middle and lower classes of the people in terms of concentrating funds. Even more grassroots banks send people to schools and factories to absorb the surplus savings of students and workers. However, when we observe banks distributing funds, we have not seen such widespread grassroots efforts. Especially in the current era of extreme economic panic in China, we only hear about banks tightening loans. What we usually see are only mortgage loans to a few large factories and large stores. As for general small factories and small businesses, they could originally rely on credit loans from money shops to survive, but what about now! The market is different, and the times have changed. The money shops themselves are experiencing difficulties. Where else can they get credit loans from? As a result, the market downturn is even worse, and commerce is declining. We only see stores closing down, and rarely see new ones opening. There is also a general public who rely solely on salaries or wages to make a living. They are also affected by the economic panic, and at the same time, the cost of living is increasing day by day. It is not easy for them to maintain their daily lives. If they occasionally encounter some unexpected accidents or have legitimate uses for money, they are helpless. Thus, they are subjected to usurious loans, high-interest rates, and various kinds of heavy exploitation. Everyone knows that they cannot fall into this trap, but when they are helpless, they have no choice but to bite the bullet and borrow. As a result, economic pressure increases day by day. When they reach the point where they can no longer cope, the strong take risks, and the suffering of the weak cannot be fully described. This situation is, of course, most developed and obvious in cities. Therefore, a small number of banks in Shanghai, in view of this situation, created small-amount credit loans to relieve the urgent needs of those who live on salaries and small factories and small businesses. This is the origin of small-amount credit loans.

Small-amount credit loans have actually been popular abroad for a long time. Even in the United States, many very ordinary banks offer millions in small-amount credit loans. It is not surprising. Many entrepreneurs also use small-amount credit loans to promote their products. We only need to look at the recent transactions of cars, radios, and bicycles, all of which have installment payment methods. This is a variation of small-amount credit loans. The Shanghai Commercial & Savings Bank's Jing'an Temple Road branch was the first bank in Shanghai to handle small-amount credit loans, opening in February 1930. Later, in April 1933, the Siming Savings Society and the Intermediate Credit Trust Company also opened and engaged in small-amount credit loan business. Later, the Xinhua Trust & Savings Bank, the Nanshi Commercial Bank, the Yongda Bank, the Tongyi Trust Company (which has been liquidated), the Ningbo Industrial Bank, and many privately organized institutions all handled small-amount credit loans. To date, there are no fewer than a dozen such institutions.

Looking at the articles of association of the lending institutions, there are generally the following common points.

(1) Borrower Qualifications - Any citizen residing in Shanghai, over the age of 21, who has been employed in a company or store for six months or operating a business for more than one year, can enjoy this service.

(2) Loan Amount - Mostly from 50 yuan to 500 yuan, occasionally some from 100 yuan to 500 yuan or 1,000 yuan.

(3) Interest - Interest rates are mostly between 6 and 9 percent per month, calculated daily, and deducted in advance when the loan is established.

(4) Loan Period - The maximum repayment period is one year, with equal monthly installments. For example, if you borrow 120 yuan, you must repay 10 yuan per month. Therefore, this type of repayment must be paid on a fixed date. If the end of the month is set as the repayment date, then it must be repaid at the end of the month without delay.

(5) Collateral - Most require two guarantors, whose qualifications are similar to those of the borrower. The guarantors are jointly and severally liable for the outstanding loan.

(6) Investigation Fee - When applying for a loan, the borrower must rely on the bank to investigate credit, so this investigation fee must also be borne by the borrower. The amount is usually 1% of the loan amount deducted when the loan is established, and some are pre-paid when applying for the loan.

(7) Overdue Repayment - As mentioned earlier, this type of loan must be repaid on a predetermined date. However, if the borrower fails to pay on time, the bank must charge a handling fee and overdue interest. The handling fee is at least 5 jiao and at most 1 yuan, and the overdue interest is calculated at 1 percent per month.

(8) Early Repayment - Borrowers can pay off all of their debts one day before the stipulated date and get a refund on part of the interest.

(9) Loan Procedures - The borrower first contacts the bank and must be questioned orally by the bank. If it is considered that the qualifications are still met, then a "loan application form" will be issued immediately. The borrower can then invite the guarantor to fill it out in detail and submit it to the bank for investigation. Then, the bank will directly notify whether the loan is approved or not. The general procedures are as described above.

(III) A Review of the Content of Small-Amount Credit Loans

Small-amount credit loans are based on the principle of installment repayment and secured by credit. Therefore, it is felt that the borrower has the following benefits:

(1) Credit Guarantee - In terms of the current situation in China, credit loans from money shops have been eliminated by the times. Credit loans from ordinary banks are only available to a small number of reputable and well-established stores. Therefore, it is not possible for individuals or small businesses to enjoy this preferential treatment. Now, as long as there are two guarantors, they can enjoy this right. This is tantamount to improving the economic status and credit of the people.

(2) Installment Payment - This type of loan uses the method of installment repayment. On the borrower's side, they only need to repay a fraction of the loan amount each month, and naturally, they will pay off the entire loan without realizing it.

(3) Cultivate a Habit of Honesty - These loans all stipulate that payments must be made every day or can be delayed for a few days. If the payment is made after the set date, a penalty (handling fee) must be paid. Therefore, the borrower must repay on time, which subtly cultivates the borrower's habit of honesty.

(4) Develop a Habit of Saving - According to the method of installment repayment, the borrower repays the debt without realizing it. Then, in the future, they can finally accumulate small amounts of savings every month to prepare for future emergencies. Isn't this cultivating a habit of saving!

Then, the bank also has the following benefits:

(1) Capital Flow - The thing that stores and banks fear the most is the inability of capital to flow. Banks are institutions that regulate finance. They should naturally pay more attention to the flow of capital. In the past, we often saw banks going bankrupt and banks being liquidated. In fact, they were not all overly indebted, and the inability of capital to flow was a major reason. Therefore, banks have recently been doing less real estate mortgage loans, which is also a significant example. However, this type of small-amount credit loan is suitable for the bank's appetite. They lend out funds and receive them back every month. Therefore, they can lend and collect at any time. This kind of continuous flow can expand business and circulate funds.

(2) Generous Interest - Looking at the current lending institutions, the interest rate on the surface is only 6 to 9 percent per month, but in reality, it is more than 15 percent per month (the calculation method is detailed later). The highest interest rate for ordinary loans is only about 10 percent, so a large amount of interest can be obtained from small-amount credit loans.

(3) Solid Creditor's Rights -

1. For this type of loan, at least two guarantors are required, and they must be jointly and severally liable with the borrower. Therefore, even if something happens to one of the three, it is not difficult to find someone to compensate among the other two.

2. This type of loan mostly stipulates a "penalty fee." This means that if the borrower fails to repay in the future, the borrower should bear the losses suffered by the bank in recovering the debt. The penalty fee is calculated at 20% of the loan amount.

3. Short Period - Generally, the repayment period for small loans now is mostly no more than one year, so the time is also shorter than other loans.

The above is said in general. If we further explore the methods, there are also places that can be studied.

(1) Interest Rate is Too High - Although the current interest rate for credit loans is between 6 and 9 percent per month, if you calculate it in detail, you feel that the interest rate for loans is too high. Now, let's give an example to illustrate:

Suppose you borrow 100 yuan from the same bank, and the interest rate is calculated at 7.5 percent per month on a daily basis. Then, the interest to be deducted for one year (365 days) is 9 yuan and 1 jiao and 3 fen, so the bank actually lends out only 90 yuan, 8 jiao, and 7 fen (100 - 9.13 = 90.87). At the end of the first month, the borrower repays 8 yuan and 3 jiao and 3 fen, so at the end of the first month, the principal lent out by the bank is only 82 yuan and 5 jiao and 4 fen (90.87 - 8.33 = 82.54). Extrapolating this way, we list the table as follows:

Time Bank's Principal Loan Amount

Initial loan of 100 yuan (deducting interest) 90.87

End of the first month 82.54 End of the second month 74.21 End of the third month 65.88

End of the fourth month 57.55 End of the fifth month 49.22 End of the sixth month 40.89

End of the seventh month 32.56 End of the eighth month 24.33 End of the ninth month 15.90 End of the tenth month 7.57

End of the eleventh month (reduced by 0.76)

Suppose we average the bank's principal loan amount

So we calculate several interest rates and get the following table, all based on a loan of 100 yuan with a term of 12 months as the calculation standard

(2) Interest Deducted in Advance - According to ordinary loans, except for the discount interest, the interest is mostly returned together with the outstanding loan. However, the interest on this small loan must also be deducted first. There is no reason for this on the bank's side. Therefore, those who do not understand the truth even say it is exploitation and extortion. However, looking at the current interest rate, it seems to be lighter than the interest rate of usurious loans on the market. If the interest rate can be further reduced, and the interest receivable is repaid in installments along with the principal, it seems more reasonable, which is lighter for the borrower and still does not cause any loss to the bank.

(3) Repayment Period is Too Short - The term for small-amount credit loans is mostly one year. If a person with a monthly salary of about 100 yuan borrows 300 yuan, then they must repay 25 yuan each time. Therefore, they must use a quarter of their salary each month to repay the loan, which will definitely make it difficult to cope with their personal or family life. As a result, they borrow here and there, and their debts become deeper and deeper. Therefore, if the loan term can be extended to one and a half or two years, the borrower's monthly burden will be reduced, and it will be easier to cope with.

(4) Conclusion

The above discussion is only a discussion of the principles and methods of small-amount credit loans. Although we have raised points that should be improved, in general, small-amount credit loans have made no small contribution to promoting the virtue of honesty and cultivating the habit of saving. Moreover, this type of loan is easy to popularize among the general middle and lower classes of the people. Therefore, the bank itself can indeed show its ability to regulate finance and serve society, while the citizens can truly get a savior from the economic panic.

Chronicle

Tidbits 171

This world is cruel; it is filled with darkness, bloodshed, and contradictions.

The strong can oppress the weak, sucking their blood and eating their flesh.

In big cities, some people sell their blood for a living, forced to relinquish the most precious thing they possess, that which sustains their life, for the enjoyment of the wealthy.

On the front lines, a strong nation can aid bandits in attacking a weak nation, arbitrarily bombing others with planes and bombs, yet forbids retaliation, because that would insult them.

In the international arena, a strong nation can even use force to conquer a weak nation, seizing its land and property, and not only can the aggressor proclaim this as spreading civilization and propagating benevolent rule, but even strong nations can exchange recognition of this as "truth," and even form alliances to "re-invade."

Are we, the weak, destined to perpetually submit, with no chance of redemption?

Eulogy for Sun Yat-sen by You Lie 172

— Qian Da

Revolutionary veteran Mr. You Lie passed away shortly after arriving in Beijing, to the sorrow of all who heard of it. During his lifetime, Mr. You, along with President Sun and Chen Shaobai and Yang Heling, advocated for revolution, earning them the title of the "Four Great Bandits." With the passing of President Sun, Chen, and Yang, Mr. You became the spiritual light of the revolutionary elders. When Mr. You came to Shanghai from Hong Kong, he resided in the home of his friend Mr. Tan Haiqiu. I visited him several times, and due to the hardships of the journey at over seventy years of age, his spirit was quite weakened, causing all who saw him to worry. Later, after his health improved somewhat, he felt a deep longing for President Sun and urgently wished to visit his mausoleum in Beijing. Thus, on the night of September 23rd, accompanied by his secretary and entourage, he departed for the capital. That evening, few knew of his departure, and only I and Mr. Tan Haiqiu, among a few others, went to the station to see him off. At parting, Mr. You shook our hands warmly, saying he looked forward to seeing us again, never imagining that this would be our final farewell, a truly tragic event. After arriving in Beijing, Mr. You, on the 26th, along with Legislative Yuan member Feng Ziyou and others, held a memorial ceremony at the mausoleum. The text of the eulogy seems not yet to have appeared in the newspapers, so I am specially recording it here for the readers of our newspaper. This eulogy reflects on old friends and mourns his own life, filled with deep sorrow and emotion, leaving the reader breathless. It is no wonder that Mr. You, having read less than half, was overcome with grief, his voice choked with tears, unable to continue. The original text is as follows:

On this twenty-sixth day of September, in the twenty-fifth year of the Republic of China, I, You Lie, respectfully offer fine flowers to pay homage to the spirit of my brother, Sun Yat-sen, the President: In the past, you led Chen and Yang, and also myself; advocating for revolution, we shared joyful mornings and evenings; with shared ambitions, our hearts were filled with passion, promoting and propagating, seeking to unveil great righteousness; the initial events in Guangzhou, secret plans were leaked; traveling overseas, enduring hardships and taking bitter medicine; persevering and striving again and again, unyielding as iron; men of high ideals followed like the wind, shedding much blood, dyeing the Republic, overthrowing the Qing dynasty; your accomplishments, who dares to steal; upholding the law and raising armies, establishing a government in Southern Yue; invited to participate in great plans, facing slander and chewing; only one meeting, becoming a permanent farewell. The burial mound is enshrined, regretting not being present at the burial; weeping and wailing, a close friend's string is broken; alas, how painful! Heling and Shaobai, one after another collapsing; looking at this one body, a lonely and desolate shape; especially encountering national hardship, increasingly severe; having seen so much suffering, my spirit is filled with sorrow; the purple gold smokes, the pine and cypress are covered in snow; coming now to mourn you, how can I bear this grief; offering flowers and pouring wine, may you enjoy this fragrance and purity; may you partake!

The Standard Cuckoo Clock 173

— Fan Xianwei

The "standard cuckoo clock" I am referring to here is not the standard time clock at the Jianghai Customs House by the Huangpu River, which reports the time every day, but a completely authentic, old-brand "goody-goody" teacher in the countryside. His surname was Hu, and his given name was Cheng. It is said that the origin of this elegant nickname was not accidental. Because when he was teaching, he didn't wear a watch. After a certain amount of time had passed, he didn't need to peek at the clock, nor did he need the school servant to ring the bell. He would, without being early or late, precisely and appropriately call the class leader to announce the end of class; therefore, the teachers in other grades, as long as they saw him stepping out of the classroom door, would also end their classes, without a second's difference. He was truly as accurate as could be.

He liked to drink alcohol and take snuff. His nose was always smeared black. Besides teaching, he also served as a local security chief. Once, he had a disagreement with the district chief. The district chief secretly pried off the plaque at his door that read "×th Bao (neighborhood unit) Security Chief's Office," intending to remove him from his post. It was very comical! At the time, he pretended not to know anything and went to the Public Security Bureau to report that the security chief's plaque had been stolen, causing a laughing matter. So people also called him the "plaque-prying security chief."

He was very honest and consistent in his work. However, because he was too consistent, he almost broke his rice bowl! I remember one autumn when school superintendents from various counties in the province were inspecting each other's schools, one superintendent arrived in the village on a Sunday, which was normally a day off from school. Unexpectedly, the superintendent had a strange idea and insisted that he gather the students at the school to give a class for him to see, saving him from having to come back and forth. At the time, he firmly refused! He just sat in the teahouse, drinking wine and listening to the superintendent. Who knew that in less than two months, the education bureau's "××××" order arrived. In fact, having classes on Sundays was something unheard of before the Song Dynasty!

Winter Goldfish 175

— Zheng Yimei

For goldfish raised delicately, one must pay attention to how they are cared for in the winter. Otherwise, goldfish are very susceptible to the problem of loosening scales due to stimulation from the cold. Or the fish's body develops spots, gradually festering, like people suffering from frostbite. To avoid this kind of problem, one must provide winter protection. The method for winter protection is to bury the fishbowl halfway in the soil, and cover the surface of the bowl with a thick reed mat at night to avoid frost and snow. The four sides of the bowl should be surrounded with rice straw. At this time, the fish has entered a semi-dormant state, and its appetite has sharply decreased. Even if you don't feed it, it won't starve to death. If it has already caught a cold, then quickly move it to the sunlight so that it receives a good amount of heat, or illuminating it with an electric lamp is also very beneficial.

Yesterday I met with Mr. Han Jiyin, who is a goldfish expert. His special garden is located west of the Shanghai South City Xietu Road Public Security Bureau gate, occupying several acres, with dozens of fishbowls. It is called "Fei Garden." I had the opportunity to visit it once in the summer. There are many famous varieties, truly rare specimens. This time, when I met him, I asked, "How are the fish in Fei Garden doing?" He said, "Taking care of goldfish in the winter is very troublesome. The fish that come from the north can still withstand the cold. Fish like the pearlscale goldfish come from the south and will freeze to death if they get a little cold." So every day near noon, he must scoop out the water from the fishbowl, making it very shallow, so that the sunlight can be more effective. In the afternoon, he gradually fills the water up again, so that when it freezes at night, only a layer of ice forms on the surface, and the fish hibernates below, not affected at all. Removing the ice the next morning is also very easy. In winter, the water doesn't easily become dirty, so it's not necessary to change it often. If you do change it, the new water must be slightly warmer than the old water, otherwise the fish will also get sick. He spares no effort in collecting rare varieties. Recently, he has added "blue telescope eye goldfish," "blue dragon egg goldfish," "blue lionhead goldfish," and "calico lionhead goldfish." A friend from the north has "violet pompom goldfish," which he envied terribly. He asked the friend to sell it to him, but the friend couldn't bear to part with it. He knew that the friend was addicted to painting, so he sent him a Pan Yisheng painting of a beautiful woman from his collection. The friend then gave him some "violet pompom goldfish" as a reward. Now they are being raised in Fei Garden. Every Saturday and Sunday, he is sure to be in the garden, receiving goldfish enthusiasts, and he invited me to come and appreciate them again, saying that the host of the Violet Society would certainly like the "violet pompom goldfish," and it would be especially welcome if I could come with him.

The Mated Phoenix Returns to its Nest 177

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter Nine: Tragic News Startles Like a Flower Falling into Filth, Frequent Visits Leave the Heart Like Floss Soaked in Mud

Guoqi said: "I said long ago that you were very generous. Of course, this is your chivalrous spirit, but..." He drew out his words, preparing to say something more tactful. He couldn't think of that sentence for a moment, so he looked at the sliver of sunlight visible through the curtain and the window. Youmei said: "But Cousin didn't expect him to have such a background, right? I originally didn't want to tell you this, but Menglan thought it wasn't appropriate to put this matter in writing, and he didn't want to deceive anyone, so he indicated to me, asking me to tell you. I thought it would be good to tell Cousin. This proves that we have a relationship of righteousness. Moreover, you'll understand how to comfort such a literary confidant." Guoqi smiled slightly for no reason and sighed again. Youmei said: "As for that ring, it was entirely my idea. I thought that correspondence relying entirely on the mail was too inappropriate. I was willing to come out and pass on news between the two sides. But to allow me to send messages between the two sides, there must be something to bring to you that can prove it. Naturally, I am a relative on one side and the best classmate on the other. I also hope that the friendship between the two of you will be even stronger. What are Cousin's thoughts?" Guoqi said: "I wrote to Miss Jiang first. Although I can't help her with anything, I can't increase her pain. I originally prepared a little something to respond to her. So it seems I don't need to send it." Youmei said: "Why? Is Cousin very upset after receiving this news?" Guoqi said: "In his writing, I knew long ago that she was an unfortunate woman, so we got along through literary righteousness. Since that's the case, being unhappy after receiving this news is just feeling sorry for him. It's definitely not because I myself am unhappy. The reason I wanted to send something to him was to give him a memento, but now I feel that he doesn't need a memento." As the conversation reached this point, the atmosphere felt very tense, but Guoqi's behavior was very leisurely. He took out a fan with a Xiangfei bamboo handle from the desk drawer, opened it, and slowly fanned himself in front of his chest. Although that fan was something he often used, he looked at the calligraphy and painting on the fan as if he were seeing it for the first time. He waved the fan a few times and then held the fan up to look at it. Although there was a look of panic on his face, he used the act of looking at the fan to cover up this panic. Youmei sat diagonally across from him, also taking a handkerchief tucked into the buttonhole under her arm and folding it smoothly on her lap. Her apple-like cheeks also took on an extra layer of red. She lowered her eyelids. She suddenly smiled and said: "What I'm saying seems meddlesome. But Miss Jiang asked me to tell Cousin about her background, so I had to say it." (109)

Transgenderism (Part 1) 178

— Pei Ming

The matter of transgenderism truly occupies an extremely important and novel page in the history of modern medicine. If there weren't factual evidence, no one would believe that such a thing really happened, and they would definitely think it was a fabricated and baseless tale. Years ago, an elderly man from Tianjin announced that his granddaughter had suddenly turned into a boy, causing a sensation and spreading as a bizarre story, but its secret was immediately revealed. In reality, this old man was just trying to use this to swindle travel expenses. But in foreign countries, there have indeed been confirmed cases of transgenderism. Here are some stories of these transsexuals:

In Warsaw, Poland, there was a 24-year-old young man named Nochmen Tenenbaum. A few years ago, he joined the army and rose to the rank of sergeant. He was also awarded several medals for bravely saving lives. Gradually, he turned into a woman and fell in love with an artist. Recently, she entered the Warsaw obstetrics hospital and told the doctor that she was about to have a baby. Four days later, Miss Nochmen Tenenbaum indeed gave birth to a perfectly healthy nine-pound baby. The artist was very happy and said that he would marry her after she recovered.

Those who like sports will not forget Miss Zdenek Koubkova, a Czech female sprinter. She was the world record holder for the women's 800-meter race. After three surgeries, she became Mr. Zdenek Koubek.

Rambling Thoughts

Thinking of the Patriotic Story of Donating Clothes to Soldiers from the Tang Palace Inspired by the Clothing Donation Movement 179

— Rushan

Seeing the proposal in this newspaper to donate over ten thousand woolen coats to support Sui, I feel that this is the most meaningful and effective way to support Sui. Donors don't feel it's a burden, and it meets the urgent needs of the soldiers. The procedures are also relatively universalized and rationalized. This is a suggestion that the Support Sui Association should adopt.

This clothing donation movement reminds me of a moving story from the Tang Dynasty when the nation's power was being extended. It shows that comforting soldiers resisting the enemy with warm clothing was already practiced in ancient times. The martial spirit of the Tang Dynasty represents the most glorious page in the history of the Chinese nation. The expansion of territory under alien rule during the Yuan and early Qing dynasties cannot be compared to the spirit of national self-respect of the Tang Dynasty. The crisis faced by the Han people in the Tang Dynasty after the Five Barbarians' Rebellion was similar to our country's present precarious situation. The spirit of national self-defense under external threats must have been very high. This can be seen in the Tang Dynasty's conscription system, where the entire nation was armed to defend the country. The bravery of Xue Rengui, Guo Ziyi, and others is still praised today in legends. What I want to mention is how the soldiers who fought bitterly in the northern frontier were treated. The main idea of the story is: the border guards' winter clothing was personally sewn by the palace ladies on the emperor's orders. One of the palace ladies, due to the loneliness of being confined to the palace for a long time and admiring the bravery of the border soldiers, couldn't help but write a love poem, which she slipped into the quilted coat for any soldier to wear, promising to become his wife in the next life. That was a kind of infatuation under impossible circumstances, but how could the soldier who found this poem dare to accept the coat? So he presented it to the imperial palace for the emperor to decide. As a result, the Tang emperor not only did not punish her, but instead betrothed the palace lady to the soldier as an encouragement. This story is not only a heartwarming tale created by the Tang emperor's joy, but in fact includes a very important meaning: first, how soldiers under the conscription system, especially those defending the border, were worshiped in the public's mind; second, why the soldiers' winter clothing was not purchased from the people, but had to be personally sewn by the palace ladies, which indicated the Tang emperor's generous treatment of the soldiers and encouraged the spirit of defending the country. As for the marriage, it was just an opportunity to show how the Tang emperor valued warriors and despised beauties from a national standpoint. We can imagine how moved the soldiers were at that time and how much more their patriotic spirit was inspired.

Now the Chinese nation is oppressed by foreign insults to a greater extent than in the Tang Dynasty. At this critical moment for national security, the people are the masters of the country. Shouldn't they care about the hard-fought spirit of the border guards? Therefore, in saving on expenses, food, and clothing, it can be said that it is a matter of course and duty to support the Sui army. At the same time, inspired by the above story, I believe that in addition to material assistance, the border guards also need spiritual encouragement. They don't have time to read newspapers and cannot directly feel the widespread sympathy of the people of the country. If we can donate 100,000 woolen coats (even if they are old), it will not only increase their ability to resist the cold in the trenches, but also make them feel directly that there are 100,000 people in the rear who are donating their clothes, and that they were woven by 100,000 women. Although they are not worth much money, they are all inner garments that everyone cherishes very much. They are actually being transferred thousands of miles to the border guards. Each garment carries infinite patriotic enthusiasm. This kind of spiritual moving power is greater than all assistance. I hope that the Support Sui Association will not neglect the spiritual effect of this clothing donation movement and adopt it carefully in addition to soliciting donations of money, so that it can be implemented quickly.
