Daily News on Sino-Japanese Relations 180

— Tian Yu

On the 9th, this newspaper translated and published a Japanese Shanghai Daily editorial on Sino-Japanese relations, criticizing the mistakes in Japan's self-proclaimed "China experts'" understanding of China. An important sentence read: "Can one expect results from looking down on one's opponent while trying to promote cooperation and friendship? ... The fact is, they are discussing China with the mindset of twenty or thirty years ago, which is no longer the case." In the past, Japanese political commentator Takashin Murobuse visited China and also published a paper on Sino-Japanese relations, arguing that the Japanese military's aggressive entry into China was a mistake, echoing our advocacy of resistance fifty years later, intending to use soft methods to make the Chinese people naturally accept their benevolent rule. This view was welcomed by some in our country who only seek immediate pleasure, unanimously praising Murobuse's remarks as "correct." Now, although the Shanghai Daily has not advised the Japanese military to use soft methods to make the Chinese people naturally accept their benevolent rule, the fact that it can criticize Japanese policy as a mistake at this time and place is enough to make us "feel flattered."

The Shanghai Daily points out that today's China is not the China of twenty or thirty years ago, a statement we believe to be correct. However, what it considers to be different is not necessarily what we consider to be different. For example, the fact that young Chinese people no longer smoke opium does not represent the distinguishing feature between today's China and the China of the past. For instance, in the past twenty or thirty years, the general Chinese populace has deeply learned from Japan's military force, especially since the September 18th Incident, this painful realization is too profound. Just this one instance of the entire nation, from top to bottom, near and far, unanimously and spontaneously assisting the Suiyuan anti-bandit campaign with the greatest enthusiasm, would never have happened in China twenty or thirty years ago. This is still a small beginning, and if expanded, the great force of the people hidden beneath the Chinese earth is inexhaustible. Perhaps precisely because of this, some more intelligent commentators from friendly countries have had to advise the Japanese military to be more careful about their steps. We are about to further expand this great force of the people, so that the invaders themselves realize that the path they are taking is a dead end!

However, the China experts from friendly countries also have some areas where they have not made mistakes. For example, using people like Zheng Xiaoxu and Yin Rugeng to indirectly rule China is the smartest method, which has been implemented and has achieved great results, and can be used forever. The Shanghai Daily did not point this out, and we are worthy to supplement this explanation here.

There is no need for the Chinese and Japanese people to hate each other. We know that the general Japanese public also sympathizes with our country being invaded. The major barrier between the two great nations is a small number of selfish people at the top of society. We welcome with the greatest respect enlightened intellectuals from friendly countries who strive to break through this barrier. However, in the past four or five years, in all newspapers and magazines of friendly countries (except for confidential ones), we have only seen writings that more or less promote aggression, or at most, remain silent. Where have the hopeful intellectuals of Japan gone?

Seafaring 181

— Meng Hua

February, the Bohai Sea thaws. Ice floes floating on the sea surface collide with each other in the howling north wind. The ship's whistle blares three sharp calls, and the ship weighs anchor.

The people clustered on the pier, their chaotic voices, as well as the distant vehicles, warehouses, and towering chimneys, all gradually recede into the distance. Enshrouded in the thin mist, the people on the shore look like ghosts, but the lights of dusk are like giant eyes filled with tears. Our ship slowly sets sail, heading towards Dalian.

At the bow, the sea waves roar, constantly splashing icy water droplets onto the deck. We all squat on the deck. Among them, several people with rolls of cotton batting under their arms and bundles on their backs are squatting near the iron railing, using a stubborn posture to resist the biting sea wind. The electric lights have not yet been turned on, and the deck is in darkness. The wind shelter flaps continuously in the wind.

I am the only person on the deck with a suitcase. In the crowd, people look at me with envious and surprised eyes. Near me, a farmer with a long, greasy pipe in his mouth constantly spews out pungent smoke at me. I occasionally glance at them, and every time he avoids my gaze. When I take out a cigarette and borrow a match from him, he asks me in a low voice with a "er" sound at the end of his sentences:

"Are you going to Guandong? You are..."

"No, I am going to Qingdao and will visit a friend in Dalian."

"You are studying in Beijing City? Eh?"

"Yes. There are fewer people going to Dalian this year, isn't that right?"

"No, there are many. Tens of thousands of people are going to Guandong. Guandong is a good place, a place for us to eat! But I heard that many people were driven away this year, and some have no news at all. I heard..." He leaned in and said softly, "Many people were killed, but none of us can stop it. We poor people, taking care of our mouths means we can't take care of our lives." As he spoke, his voice became extremely somber.

"How old are you this year..."

"Oh, fifty-eight. After fifty, there's not much time left! Living one day counts as one day. Don't you think so?"

"Do you need to run to Guandong to find work? I heard that Guandong has been very dangerous lately."

"That's right, you don't need to run to Guandong to find work. I look for work everywhere in Beijing City and Jinan Prefecture all year round, but is there any? Guandong is still the old place, a familiar road is better than a strange road. Dangerous? Sigh, there's no controlling so many things in the world now."

I am silent. Every word of the old man hits my heart. I raise my head. The ship has already sailed out of the harbor. Outside the railing is an infinite darkness. The mainmast standing firmly in the middle of the ship, its tip seems to be inserted into the dark clouds of the sky. The sea is rolling even more powerfully.

Most of the people around have fallen asleep, and some are even emitting a low snore. Some tremble constantly when they sleep, and the snore sounds like a patient's groan.

"You are wearing too little, it must be cold, right?" I ask.

"Yeah! A little. Tonight's sea wind is really strange, like it has thorns! Sigh. But, I've had enough of the cold. One winter, some of our brothers were working as miners in the Fushun pit, and it was freezing to death. It snowed heavily for three nights in a row, and the shed collapsed. Several brothers froze to death that time. I only remember being so frozen that I couldn't move, and I couldn't even shout for help, as if a ghost was covering my mouth with its hand. The next morning, the brothers in the same pit rescued us. Since then, I couldn't work anymore. Then I transferred to Harbin and worked in the White Russian factory for exactly three years. Until September 18th. Three years, exactly three years, when I left the factory, I didn't even have a penny! Sigh. The White Russians and the Yellow Russians are all the same ruthless, the brothers all said so." He sighed a long breath. "Many of the brothers who came out together are all gone now, it's really..." He lowered his head. We didn't say anything, and deathly silence occupied the entire deck.

The noise of the machines accompanied the northeast wind, howling wildly. We are all trembling.

Suddenly, the old man leaned forward, moved to my side, and said to me in a low voice:

"Sir, you are a scholar, tell me, when can we have our day? Haven't we suffered enough from the Yellow Russians?" He looked at me with wide eyes, and I shivered all over.

On the deck and on the sea, there is still an endless darkness. In the far distance, the light of the lighthouse seems to appear and disappear as it searches.

Boxing 182

— Yin Fei

A Friend's Letter

Friend: I am too excited. After watching the boxing match, as I dispersed with the crowd to the entrance, I realized that my hands were all sweaty, and my face was burning hot. When the wind blew, I didn't feel its cold, but it felt strangely good and comfortable.

Excitedly returning home, excitedly getting into bed, spending a lot of effort, and taking more than an hour, I finally fell asleep. But after falling asleep, I was awakened by my overly excited nerves. I had a dream.

I dreamed that I was also a boxer. My opponent was much taller and stronger than me. Therefore, I only had time to parry and no chance to counterattack. But even parrying, I couldn't parry. I was beaten with a face full of blood, but I still couldn't help but parry, because not parrying would lead to being beaten even more severely. The opponent would never stop attacking just because you were bleeding. I could only desperately parry, taking the opportunity to swing my small fist and strike at the opponent bravely. Although some strikes missed, sometimes I could hit him, and I was so happy to see blood flowing from his face that I laughed and woke up.

After waking up, I unconsciously touched my face. Was my face hot? Just like when I came out of the boxing match. Subconsciously, I looked at my hands to see if there was any blood? But there wasn't. I realized that I was just dreaming, and I was sleeping in a warm quilt. However, the shouts of the onlookers are still ringing in my ears, and those shouts were to encourage the strong to attack, not to sympathize with the weak. When one side suffered a heavy blow, the shouts rose from all around. They didn't favor one side, as long as you could beat the other side, the shout would be for you. This crazy-like shouting is ringing in my ears now, but I can't tell whether this is intimidating me or encouraging me?

It is midnight now, and there is probably still some time before dawn? The weather is very cold again. After writing these, I want to go back to sleep. Will I still have boxing dreams after sleeping? I don't know. Let me have them. I will gladly have them. I am not afraid of such dreams now. Even if I get beaten until my head is broken and bleeding again, I will continue to fight, because I understand the reason why I must continue to fight: not fighting will lead to being beaten even more.

That crazy shouting is ringing again. Now that I hear this sound, I feel it is a bit lovely. It is not a temptation, but it is a threat, and it can also be said that it is a warning.

It warns the weak that they must fight on!

Beacon Fire 183

— Zhu Lu

——Remembering Badaling

When the train, like a snake, passed through three tunnels, the belt-like Juyongguan fell behind, and the train arrived at Qinglongqiao and stopped in the valley.

The wind and sand of the northern country are world-famous. When stepping on the gravel, running up the slope, crossing the stone steps, and climbing up the Great Wall, the wind and sand outside the Great Wall blow particularly hard, causing the traveler's clothes to make a rustling sound. The strong wind stirs up sand and dust, making the sky also hazy.

Walking on the Great Wall, stepping on the large stone bricks, many bricks on the city wall are incomplete. The Great Wall rises and falls like big waves. When a gust of wind and sand blows, the mountains seem to be in a mist.

Looking at the slope from the city, there is a village in the desolate, deep yellow sand.

When running up a watchtower, leaning against the gap, looking at the seemingly boundless outside the fort, the boundless, desolate desert unfolds. In the deep yellow sand, several shepherds are looking for food for their livestock. In a vast, desolate desert, several cargo merchants pace like shadows, leading groups of camels—the kings of the desert—with heavy bundles stacked on their humps, slowly shaking their heads, walking step by step towards the desert with swaying movements.

The winding Great Wall, undulating and lying on the top of the mountain, seems to extend deep into the hazy clouds. The lofty and solemn eight high mountain peaks stand like castles high in the sky. Many mountains surround it like sand dunes.

Page 18

The mountains are covered with fine wild grass that undulates in the wind. When the wind and sand blow, a layer of gray sand covers the sky.

A traveler crossed the city bricks, struck a match, and with great difficulty avoided the wind, striking several matches before finally using the fire to light the overgrown wild grass. A wisp of light smoke floated up, and the faint fire spread. The light smoke slowly thickened, like an ancient beacon fire, and black smoke rose up, slowly rising even more. The black smoke, like the tongue of a snake, licked the sky...

This is something I will never forget. Whenever I think of the solemn Badaling, the beacon fire seems to appear before my eyes—I hope that the beacon fire will burn forever, that the black smoke can rush up to the sky, like a burning torch in the darkness, forever illuminating the earth.

Shentonya 184

— Lei Shiyu

"Shentonya" is a transliteration. Except that the character "ya" can be translated as "ya" (this "ya" does not mean house, but is a term for generally lower-class merchants, such as calling newspaper vendors "news ya," calling laundrymen "laundry ya," but also calling children "fang ya"...), the first two characters are quite difficult to find a name with the same meaning to replace them, because it is a special Japanese proper noun. I originally wanted to use the words "officially transmitted advertisement person," but China does not use that method to publicize advertisements, and there are many ways to promote them.

, what kind of guys are they after all?

I believe that people who go to Tokyo have seen this strange sight several times in at least one month, especially in prosperous areas. But I didn't know the name until I had been in Tokyo for more than a year. If I hadn't looked it up in the dictionary after reading a novel, or asked someone or heard someone tell it, I might not understand it even now.

The strange sight is this: a group of strangely shaped people (at least three or more), there are men and women in the crowd, but if you don't distinguish by sound, you might see men as women, and women as men. Because they (she) almost all wear the same strange clothes, and the foundation smeared on their faces is almost several times thicker than that of prostitutes, and they also use something jet black to draw their eyebrows extra thick and long. Some even put a few strokes somewhere on their faces, such as a mustache on their mouths. Although their tasks are the same, they are divided in cooperation. For example, some play cymbals, some blow pipes or trumpets, some beat drums, and some leave the team to hand out advertisements. The most important thing is the leader at the front who holds up something like an umbrella, on which is written in large, special characters an advertisement for either a discount or an opening. His steps seem to have taken a lot of effort to study. I'm sorry I can't describe it, but this impression still remains in my mind: those two feet tap very quickly, but they walk very slowly, and they step in an arc. His step movements are in harmony with the drum music, and the advertisement banner also moves left or right, or slightly rises or falls in harmony with his step movements. Once, I was walking on the street with Hideo Koizumi and happened to meet such a team. Koizumi admired that person's steps very much, and while staring at him, he repeatedly said:

"Very skilled, what good steps those are!"

I interrupted disapprovingly:

"What is that all about? If you play that, you might be even better than him."

"No, that's very difficult to learn!" He said seriously, as if he was sincerely admiring, and at the same time looked back at him again and again.

The individual actions of the people behind are different, but the steps are very consistent.

There are many ways to advertise, and they are improving day by day, for example, some use balloons, some use airplanes..., but this kind of Japanese "Shentonya" still exists, perhaps because it still retains a kind of charm to attract business. (Tokyo Miscellany)

Storytelling 186

Cao Xiaoying "Jade Dragonfly"

China and West (1040) 1:00 PM to 1:45 PM

Opening "Liu Bei"

Descendant of Prince Jing of Zhongshan in the Han Dynasty. Imperial Uncle known throughout the world. Extraordinary appearance, born poor. How could his ambitions be fulfilled in his life? Three brothers swore brotherhood in the Peach Garden. Praying to the gods, they will not betray the oath. Working together to sweep away the Yellow Turbans. Wearing cloth clothes, they are inevitably despised. A weaver of mats and a maker of shoes. Given official positions for their merits in Anxi County. Shook his name with might at Hulao Pass. Relying on Yuan Shao and Liu Biao. Not a match for Cao Cao's million soldiers. Temporarily lodged in Jingzhou. Then went to Wu for marriage. Brother-in-law always harbored enemy intentions. After that, he entered Sichuan and became the Shu Han. Actually formed a tripartite balance of power. Military advisor, Mr. Zhuge's plan. Persuading the officials to present a memorial. Because Cao Pi called himself emperor, he also became a ruler. Guan and Zhang were harmed, and Jingxiang was lost. Helplessly, the linked camps were burned by fire. Entrusted the orphan in his illness to support the young lord. Liu Chan was over forty years old. He lived his life as the King of Anle. Composed by Master Zhu into a program. The Shu Han finally became the orthodox ruler. Respectfully supporting the small court of the Southern Song Dynasty.

He Yunfang and He Qinfang "Double Pearl Ball"

Yuan Chang (1120) 3:30 PM to 4:15 PM Opening "Cai Wenji"

Highly talented and learned, beautiful in appearance. It is said that Wenji has her father's style. In her childhood, she could distinguish the strings on the zither. But he, accidentally overheard it from a distance. Not competing with the southern wind, she is truly intelligent. Just like Kuang, a master musician in the past. Zhonglang's daughter inherits the family's studies. Her peerless talent is like Cai Yong's. Unexpectedly, she drifted to the land of the barbarians in middle age. But she unexpectedly met Cao Cao. The wonderful thing is that she can decipher Cao Cao's hidden words. Her nephew is clear and meaningful. At that time, he did not hesitate to spend a thousand gold to redeem her. Only because he had the deepest friendship with her father in the same court. Only then was Wenji able to return to the Han country. To avoid lamenting her fate as a wanderer. But then again, she had already suffered the hardships of displacement. Not the same as ordinary ladies. Pitiable is the woman with both talent and beauty. But after all, she will have no support and no dependence in the end. In the beginning, she composed the Pipa music. Eighteen Hu Jia tunes are well-crafted. The finger sounds and techniques are exquisite. Spring rain, summer heat, autumn thoughts. Heavy snow in winter. The tune is desolate, and the rhythm is tragic. The lone swan that breaks its intestines on the flat sand knows it is not met with its soul mate.

Jiang Binchu "Three Smiles"

New Sound (1380) 7:00 PM to 8:00 PM

Opening "Ma Rong"

Born poor, but a child prodigy. Reflecting on snow and catching fireflies, he always worked hard. Brothers are often deprived of parents, without a place to live in a broken house. He doesn't complain about the difficulty of food and clothing. Suddenly, he hears the noise of people outside the door. The whole city is sending off a beautiful woman. The servants are rushing away. The scholar is so scared that he has no master. Chang'e should be in the Guanghan Palace, making a deep bow and asking in detail. My father is named Ma Rong. She is hiding in the embroidered courtyard named Yaocao. Needlework every year diligently. Wanting to dedicate treacherous power to the Liang Xiang Mansion. Determined to disobey the order. How could it be the same as ordinary unfilial sons. Intending to associate with a poor scholar, involving the talented Prime Minister Jian. If you don't dislike my ugly appearance. I am willing to cook and be a maid. Why not accompany you to read until five o'clock. Otherwise, bury my body in the gutter. I am afraid of falling into the eighteenth hell. I will never fail the Prime Minister.

Movies

Amateur Dramatists Hold Third Public Performance 188

Actively Rehearsing Recently

Since the Shanghai Amateur Dramatists performed Ibsen's "Nora" and Gogol's "The Government Inspector" last year, it can be said that they have "established" a very strong foundation in the Chinese drama world, setting off a huge wave in the lonely drama movement in recent years. The performance of "Nora" and "The Government Inspector" is also a rare harvest in the Chinese drama scene. At the beginning of 1936, they considered staging "Sai Jinhua," but due to various problems, they decided to postpone it temporarily.

It has recently been confirmed that the amateur dramatists have resolved to stage "The Power of Darkness" adapted from Tolstoy, "The Thunderstorm" by Ostrovsky, and "The Pig" adapted from the famous English drama (that is, O'Casey's "Juno and the Paycock"), three of the world's great plays, and have begun actively rehearsing on December 1, with a duration of forty days, and will hold a full rehearsal of the entire play starting on January 1.

The public performance will be in mid-January, scheduled for ten days, with each play performed for three days, and the first day will be a premiere.

"Street Angel" Begins Filming 189

Following "Hearts United in Life and Death," Yuan Muzhi is currently engaged in his new work "Street Angel," which he wrote and directed. The script has already been approved by the central government and has begun filming at the Second Factory studio, actively rushing to complete it within the old calendar year.

All the technical staff of "Street Angel" are successors from "Hearts United in Life and Death," with no changes, photography by Wu Yinxi, scenery by Ma Shouhong, and sound by Lu Yinkeng.

"Queen" Star Betty Bruce 190

A Rising Child Star: Wu Xiaozhu in "Eternal Smile" 191

Looking at the Hollywood child stars constantly appearing on the screen with their innocent and adorable performances, and then looking back at our own child stars, one can't help but sigh with a feeling of being far behind.

Child stars are often indispensable and important characters in a film's plot, and they also possess the magic to grasp the emotions of the audience. Naturally, this effect can only be achieved by child stars with talent and considerable training.

In the upcoming major production "Eternal Smile," starring Hu Die and directed by Wu Cun, there is a child star worth our attention: Wu Xiaozhu, the young daughter of director Wu Cun. In this play, her innocence, liveliness, and cleverness are fully displayed. Especially in several scenes where she appears with Hu Die, she is even more endearing. Hu Die said, "This is a promising star of the future!"

She is only ten years old this year and is studying in the fourth grade at Jingru Elementary School. Because of her intelligence, she consistently achieves excellent results in each term. When she was in the second grade at Xinya Elementary School, she won the speech championship, which shows how clever and articulate her little mouth is.

She has experience in performing stage plays. She also participated in the stage play "Crescent Moon," which Hu Die previously starred in.

Yi Hua News 192

After the success of Fang Peilin's "Sequel to Incarnation Girl," another masterpiece, "Sequel to Incarnation Girl," starring Yuan Meiyun, with Lu Ming, Wang Naidong, Han Langen, Guan Hongda, Qin Tong, Wang Guilin, Ye Wenqiu, Zhao Manna, and others in supporting roles, has been fully completed and is currently in the process of editing. It is scheduled to be screened on New Year's Day.

Yuan Meiyun in "Incarnation Girl" transformed between male and female, confusing and mesmerizing, performing with superb skill. Now, in "Sequel to Incarnation Girl," she boldly attempts to portray three different personalities, reaching a state of perfection without being bogged down. Her acting skills are outstanding and a rare achievement on the silver screen. When this film is released, it will surely cause a sensation among audiences in Shanghai.

"Crossroads" Nears Completion; Two Songs Also Approved 193

Shen Xiling's "Crossroads" is being filmed urgently these days with Lu Ban and Sha Meng. The interior scenes are about to be completed. There are still a few important exterior scenes to be filmed once the weather clears up.

The two songs in the play, "In Spring" and "Missing Hometown," have also been approved by the Film Censorship Board, it is said.

"Little Orphan Annie Comic Strip" Sells Well 194

The "Little Orphan Annie Comic Strip" published by Xinhua Film Company, drawn by cartoonist Zhang Leping, is not only superb in its brushwork and meticulous in its layout but also novel in its composition and luxuriously decorated. It also features thirty-eight expressive photos of Chen Juanjuan taken by Shi Dongshan, which are clever, adorable, and hard to come by. Currently, the company, considering the banditry and false peace in Suiyuan, and the national donations to aid the war effort, and to show patriotism, has specially offered 20,000 copies of the book, with the proceeds to be used for aid to Suiyuan. To stimulate readers' interest, the young star Chen Juanjuan personally signed the books as a souvenir. Donating to save the country is the duty of every citizen, and the book is exquisite, lovely, and inexpensive, selling for only five cents. It achieves several goals at once, benefiting both the public and private interests. In recent days, the company has been overwhelmed with inquiries and purchases of the book. The book is available at various newspaper vendors, bookstores, and cinemas. Direct mail to the company at the third floor of the Gong Stage on Edward Road is also possible.
